      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        title: >-
          Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
          highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms

          genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic

        content: >-
          Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico contexts to
          perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex
          traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
          across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
          critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
          disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
          architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
          base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.
      response:
        output: >-
          Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to execute their
          functions. A mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          varying conditions is essential to discern how these genes influence
          complex traits. This knowledge is crucial for the development of new
          therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on
          the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However,
          contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that
          gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease onset and progression.
          In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that
          integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a unified latent representation for joint analysis. This
          representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
          expression patterns under identical conditions. We found that diseases
          are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
          cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
          and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen
          to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered that functionally important
          players, although lacking associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic
          associations and uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene
          strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the perspective of gene modules.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
          role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest
          that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease onset and
          progression. This highlights a gap in our understanding, as the role
          of gene co-expression in disease etiology and drug mechanisms remains
          underexplored. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation
          for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          exhibiting similar expression patterns across identical conditions.
          Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation demonstrated
          that functionally important genes, although lacking direct
          associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a unique approach to
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          providing a more comprehensive understanding of disease etiology and
          drug mechanisms. This approach could potentially identify therapeutic
          targets overlooked by single-gene strategies, advancing the field of
          functional genomics and paving the way for drug repurposing.

        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          in specific contexts to influence complex traits is crucial for
          developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies
          have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms,
          current models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in
          disease onset and progression. This highlights a gap in our
          understanding of the complex architecture of traits and the need for a
          more comprehensive approach. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER,
          a novel computational method that integrates gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent
          representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
          modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across
          identical conditions. Our findings reveal that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
          infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of
          lipid regulation demonstrated that functionally important genes,
          although lacking direct associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          offers a unique approach to interpreting genetic associations,
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes to reveal potential
          therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. This
          advancement in genetic studies could significantly enhance our
          understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms, propelling the
          field of functional genomics forward.

          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

      response:
        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
          role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest
          that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease onset and
          progression. This highlights a gap in our understanding, as the role
          of gene co-expression in disease etiology and drug mechanisms remains
          underexplored. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation
          for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          exhibiting similar expression patterns across identical conditions.
          Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation demonstrated
          that functionally important genes, although lacking direct
          associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a unique approach to
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          thereby uncovering potential therapeutic targets overlooked by
          single-gene strategies. This advancement in genetic studies could
          significantly enhance our understanding of disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms, paving the way for more effective therapeutic strategies
          and drug repurposing.

          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.
      response:
        output: >-
          We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          unified latent representation for comprehensive analysis. Genes
          function synergistically within specific contexts, and understanding
          their influence on complex traits necessitates a mechanistic
          comprehension of expression regulation under varying conditions. This
          knowledge is vital for the development of new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in
          elucidating the role of individual genes in disease-related
          mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture
          suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease onset and
          progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is founded on modules of
          genes exhibiting similar expression patterns under identical
          conditions. We find that diseases are significantly linked to gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we
          discover that functionally significant players, although lacking
          associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In summary, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating clusters of
          co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
          potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          offers a unique framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the perspective of gene modules.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic

          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_20
      response:
        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
          role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest
          that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease origin and
          progression. However, a gap exists in our understanding of these
          interactions and their regulation across different conditions, which
          is essential for a comprehensive view of disease etiology. To address
          this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
          maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
          into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
          representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings reveal
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR
          screen analysis of lipid regulation demonstrated that functionally
          important players, although lacking direct associations, are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion,
          PhenoPLIER offers a new perspective for interpreting genetic
          associations, highlighting the importance of gene co-expression. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and uncover potential therapeutic
          targets overlooked by single-gene strategies, thereby advancing our
          understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, provides a new framework for interpreting genetic
          associations, contextualizing them, and revealing potential
          therapeutic targets that single-gene strategies may overlook. This
          approach advances our understanding of disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms, thereby contributing to the broader field of genetic
          studies.

          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          unified latent representation for comprehensive analysis. Genes
          function synergistically within specific contexts, necessitating a

          PhenoPLIER. In summary, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating clusters of
          co-expressed genes, provides a unique framework for interpreting
          genetic associations, offering insights into potential targets
          overlooked by single-gene strategies.

          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
          role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest
          that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease onset and
          progression. However, a gap exists in our understanding of these
          interactions and their regulation across different conditions, which
          is where our research comes in. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation

          new framework for interpreting genetic associations, highlighting
          potential therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.

          mechanisms, thereby contributing to the broader field of genetic
          studies and drug repurposing.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial, particularly in the context
          of developing new therapies. However, a gap exists in our mechanistic
          understanding of gene expression regulation across different
          conditions. This study addresses this gap by focusing on the
          significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types. We introduce a novel approach, PhenoPLIER,
          which accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Our results, including a CRISPR screen analysis
          of lipid regulation, reveal that functionally important players, often
          overlooked in single-gene strategies, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          provides a new framework for interpreting genetic associations through
          the lens of gene modules, thereby contextualizing genetic associations
          and uncovering potential therapeutic targets. This approach advances
          the broader field by highlighting the importance of considering gene
          co-expression in genetic studies and drug repurposing.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial, particularly in the context
          of developing new therapies. However, a gap exists in our mechanistic
          understanding of gene expression regulation across different
          conditions. This study addresses this gap by focusing on the
          significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types. We introduce a novel approach, PhenoPLIER,
          which accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Our results, including a CRISPR screen analysis
          of lipid regulation, reveal that functionally important players, often
          overlooked in single-gene strategies, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          provides a new framework for interpreting genetic associations through
          the lens of gene modules, thereby contextualizing genetic associations
          and uncovering potential therapeutic targets. This approach advances
          the broader field by highlighting the importance of considering gene
          co-expression in genetic studies and drug repurposing.

          Genes function synergistically within specific contexts to perform
          their roles. A mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation
          across varying conditions is essential to understand how these genes
          influence complex traits. This understanding is pivotal for the
          development of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have been instrumental in revealing the role of individual genes in
          disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex
          trait architecture suggest that interactions between genes are
          critical in disease onset and progression. In this study, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
          latent representation for combined analysis. This representation is
          founded on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns
          under identical conditions. We found that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. Our
          method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid
          regulation, we discovered that functionally significant players,
          although lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated
          modules by PhenoPLIER.

          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          Despite the insights gained from transcriptome-wide association
          studies on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current
          models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease

          interactions in disease progression but also highlight the potential
          of PhenoPLIER in identifying therapeutic targets and advancing drug

          functional genomics.

          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          Genes function collaboratively within specific contexts to execute
          their roles. A mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation
          across varying conditions is essential to understand how these genes
          impact complex traits. This understanding is vital for the development
          of new therapeutic strategies. Transcriptome-wide association studies

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in

          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes

          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to

        output: >-
          In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          and influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.
          Despite the insights gained from transcriptome-wide association
          studies on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, current
          models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in disease
          origin and progression, a facet not fully explored. This study
          introduces PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that bridges
          this gap by mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
          analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting
          similar expression patterns across identical conditions. Our results
          reveal that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
          expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
          known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, a
          CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation demonstrated that
          functionally important players, although lacking direct associations,
          are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These
          findings not only answer the question of gene-gene interactions in
          disease progression but also advance the field by providing a new tool
          for identifying therapeutic targets and potential drug repurposing
          opportunities.

              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic associations and

            text: >-
              In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes
              interact and influence complex traits is crucial for developing
              new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
              shed light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms,
              current models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in
              disease onset and progression. This highlights a gap in our
              understanding, as the role of gene co-expression in disease
              etiology and drug mechanisms remains underexplored. To address
              this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
              exhibiting similar expression patterns across identical
              conditions. Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types.
              PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
              regulation demonstrated that functionally important genes,
              although lacking direct associations, are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
              offers a unique approach to interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, providing a more comprehensive
              understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms. This
              approach could potentially identify therapeutic targets overlooked
              by single-gene strategies, advancing the field of functional
              genomics and paving the way for drug repurposing.

              Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to execute their
              functions. A mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
              across varying conditions is essential to discern how these genes
              influence complex traits. This knowledge is vital for the
              development of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association

              disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              pivotal in disease onset and progression. In this study, we
              present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
              expression patterns under identical conditions. We found that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered
              that functionally important genes lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
              potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the perspective of gene modules.

              have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
              representation is base on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
              significantl associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules.

              Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to execute their
              functions. A mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
              across varying conditions is essential to discern how these genes
              influence complex traits. This knowledge is crucial for the
              development of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
              studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in
              disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              pivotal in disease onset and progression. In this study, we
              present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
              expression patterns under identical conditions. We found that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered
              that functionally important genes lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
              potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the perspective of gene modules.

              ---

              We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent representation for comprehensive analysis. Genes
              function synergistically within specific contexts, and
              understanding their influence on complex traits necessitates a
              mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation under varying
              conditions. This knowledge is vital for the development of new
              therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been
              instrumental in elucidating the role of individual genes in
              disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              pivotal in disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's
              representation is founded on modules of genes exhibiting similar
              expression patterns under identical conditions. We find that
              diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover,
              using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we discover
              that functionally significant players, although lacking
              associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In summary, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating clusters of
              co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic associations and
              uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.
              PhenoPLIER offers a unique framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the perspective of gene modules.

              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes

              current models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in

              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent

              modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across the

              cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease

              We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent representation for comprehensive analysis. Genes
              function synergistically within specific contexts, and
              understanding their influence on complex traits necessitates a
              mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation under varying
              conditions. This knowledge is pivotal for the development of new
              therapeutic strategies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
              have been instrumental in elucidating the role of individual genes
              in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              vital in disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's
              representation is predicated on modules of genes exhibiting
              similar expression patterns under identical conditions. We find
              that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, a
              CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation reveals that
              functionally significant players, although lacking associations,
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              summary, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating clusters of co-expressed
              genes, provides a unique framework for interpreting genetic
              associations, offering insights into potential targets overlooked
              by single-gene strategies.

              this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
              maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
              into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
              expression patterns across identical conditions. Our findings
              reveal that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation
              demonstrated that functionally important players, although lacking
              associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a unique framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, thereby filling the gap in our understanding of gene
              co-expression in disease etiology and drug mechanisms. This
              approach advances the broader field by highlighting potential
              therapeutic targets and opportunities for drug repurposing.

              structure and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should
              follow a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1)
              The context portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper
              will fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing
              the broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
              data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis.
              Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of
              genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.
              We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              Genes function synergistically within specific contexts to perform
              their roles. A mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation

              structure and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should
              follow a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1)
              The context portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper
              will fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing
              the broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.

              Genes function synergistically within specific contexts to perform
              their roles. A mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation

              of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid

              although lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER.

              In the field of functional genomics, understanding the regulatory
              mechanisms of gene expression across different conditions is
              crucial for determining their influence on complex traits and for
              the development of new therapies. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have shed light on the role of individual
              genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest that gene-gene

              introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological

              analysis. This representation is founded on modules of genes

              conditions. Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly

              mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
              regulation demonstrated that functionally important players,
              although lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. These results not only answer the question
              of gene-gene interaction's role in disease progression but also
              highlight the potential of PhenoPLIER in identifying therapeutic
              targets and advancing drug repurposing, thereby pushing the
              boundaries of genetic studies and functional genomics.

            text: >-
              In the field of functional genomics, understanding the complex
              interplay of genes and their expression regulation across
              different conditions is crucial for elucidating disease etiology
              and developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
              studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease
              mechanisms, current models suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              pivotal in disease origin and progression, a facet not fully
              explored in existing literature. Addressing this gap, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is predicated on modules of genes exhibiting
              similar expression patterns across identical conditions. Our
              results reveal significant associations between diseases and gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER demonstrates
              accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Notably, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
              regulation revealed that functionally important players, although
              lacking direct associations, are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings underscore the potential of
              PhenoPLIER in identifying therapeutic targets and advancing drug
              repurposing efforts, thereby contributing to the broader field of
              genetic studies and complex trait clustering.

              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.

          - >-
            Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform
            their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex
            traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
            across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
            critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide
            association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
            in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
            architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
            play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
            introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
            associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
            latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
            based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
            the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
            associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
            our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
            inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen
            to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
            players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
            modules by PhenoPLIER.
